       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      In 1983
      <a href="/wiki/Project_Socrates" title="Project Socrates">
       Project Socrates
      </a>
      was initiated in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_intelligence_community" title="US intelligence community">
       US intelligence community
      </a>
      to determine the source of declining US economic and military competitiveness. Project Socrates concluded that technology exploitation is the foundation of all
      <a href="/wiki/Competitive_advantage" title="Competitive advantage">
       competitive advantage
      </a>
      and that declining US competitiveness was from decision-making in the private and public sectors switching from technology exploitation (technology-based planning) to money exploitation (economic-based planning) at the end of World War II.
     </p>
     <p>
      Project Socrates determined that to rebuild US competitiveness, decision making throughout the US had to readopt technology-based planning. Project Socrates also determined that countries like China and India had continued executing technology-based (while the US took its detour into economic-based) planning, and as a result had considerably advanced the process and were using it to build themselves into superpowers. To rebuild US competitiveness the US decision-makers needed to adopt a form of technology-based planning that was far more advanced than that used by China and India.
     </p>
     <p>
      Project Socrates determined that technology-based planning makes an evolutionary leap forward every few hundred years and the next evolutionary leap, the Automated Innovation Revolution, was poised to occur. In the Automated Innovation Revolution the process for determining how to acquire and utilize technology for a competitive advantage (which includes R&amp;D) is automated so that it can be executed with unprecedented speed, efficiency and agility.
     </p>
     <p>
      Project Socrates developed the means for automated innovation so that the US could lead the Automated Innovation Revolution in order to rebuild and maintain the country's economic competitiveness for many generations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animal_species">
       Other animal species
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Tool_use_by_animals" title="Tool use by animals">
       Tool use by animals
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Structures_built_by_animals" title="Structures built by animals">
       Structures built by animals
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_engineer" title="Ecosystem engineer">
       Ecosystem engineer
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gorilla_tool_use.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="916" data-file-width="1370" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gorilla_tool_use.png/220px-Gorilla_tool_use.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gorilla_tool_use.png/330px-Gorilla_tool_use.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gorilla_tool_use.png/440px-Gorilla_tool_use.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gorilla_tool_use.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        This adult
        <a href="/wiki/Gorilla" title="Gorilla">
         gorilla
        </a>
        uses a branch as a
        <a href="/wiki/Walking_stick" title="Walking stick">
         walking stick
        </a>
        to gauge the water's depth, an example of technology usage by non-human primates.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The use of basic technology is also a feature of other animal species apart from humans. These include primates such as
      <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee" title="Chimpanzee">
       chimpanzees
      </a>
      , some
      <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">
       dolphin
      </a>
      communities,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Crow" title="Crow">
       crows
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Considering a more generic perspective of technology as ethology of active environmental conditioning and control, we can also refer to animal examples such as beavers and their dams, or bees and their honeycombs.
     </p>
     <p>
      The ability to make and use tools was once considered a defining characteristic of the genus
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_(genus)" title="Homo (genus)">
       Homo
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the discovery of tool construction among chimpanzees and related primates has discarded the notion of the use of technology as unique to humans. For example, researchers have observed wild chimpanzees utilising tools for foraging: some of the tools used include leaf sponges, termite fishing probes,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pestle" title="Pestle">
       pestles
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lever" title="Lever">
       levers
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_African_chimpanzee" title="West African chimpanzee">
       West African chimpanzees
      </a>
      also use stone hammers and anvils for cracking nuts,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      as do
      <a href="/wiki/Capuchin_monkey" title="Capuchin monkey">
       capuchin monkeys
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Roraima" title="Boa Vista, Roraima">
       Boa Vista
      </a>
      , Brazil.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_technology">
       Future technology
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Emerging_technologies" title="Emerging technologies">
       Emerging technologies
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Theories_of_technology" title="Theories of technology">
       Theories of technology
      </a>
      often attempt to predict the future of technology based on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_technology" title="High technology">
       high technology
      </a>
      and science of the time.
     </p>
